class="mediawiki ltr sitedir-ltr mw-hide-empty-elt ns-0 ns-subject mw-editable page-Fake_news_website rootpage-Fake_news_website skin-vector action-view skin-vector-legacy"><div id="mw-page-base" CentralNotice --></div>\n\t<div class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n\t</div>\n\t<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" >Fake news website</h1>\n\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\n\t\t<div id="contentSub"></div>\n\t\t<div id="contentSub2"></div>\n\t\t\n\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>\n\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>\n\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about intentionally fraudulent websites. For satirical websites, see <a href="/wiki/News_satire" title="News satire">News satire</a>.</div>\n<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Website that deliberately publishes hoaxes and disinformation purporting to be real news</div> \n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For broader coverage of this topic, see <a href="/wiki/Fake_news" title="Fake news">Fake news</a>.</div>\n<p><b>Fake news websites</b> (also referred to as <b>hoax news websites</b>)<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> are <a href="/wiki/Internet_website" class="mw-redirect" title="Internet website">Internet websites</a> that deliberately publish <a href="/wiki/Fake_news" title="Fake news">fake news</a>\xe2\x80\x94<a href="/wiki/Hoaxes" class="mw-redirect" title="Hoaxes">hoaxes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Propaganda" title="Propaganda">propaganda</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Disinformation" title="Disinformation">disinformation</a> purporting to be <a href="/wiki/News" title="News">real news</a>\xe2\x80\x94often using <a href="/wiki/Social_media" title="Social media">social media</a> to drive <a href="/wiki/Web_traffic" title="Web traffic">web traffic</a> and amplify their effect.<sup id="cite_ref-russiadominates_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-russiadominates-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-snopesfieldguide_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-snopesfieldguide-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-divideeurope_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-divideeurope-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Unlike <a href="/wiki/News_satire" title="News satire">news satire</a>, fake news websites deliberately seek to be perceived as legitimate and taken at face value, often for financial or political gain.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-snopesfieldguide_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-snopesfieldguide-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Such sites have promoted political falsehoods in India,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Germany,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-merkelwarns_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merkelwarns-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Indonesia and the Philippines,<sup id="cite_ref-MozurScott_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MozurScott-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Sweden, Mexico,<sup id="cite_ref-concernoverbarrage_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-concernoverbarrage-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Myanmar,<sup id="cite_ref-sheerafrenkel_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sheerafrenkel-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> and the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-pbsrussianpropaganda_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbsrussianpropaganda-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-afprussianpropaganda_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afprussianpropaganda-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Many sites originate in, or are promoted by, Russia,<sup id="cite_ref-russiadominates_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-russiadominates-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-thenewyorkeradrianchen_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thenewyorkeradrianchen-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> North Macedonia,<sup id="cite_ref-tynan_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tynan-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bengilbert_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bengilbert-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Romania,<sup id="cite_ref-romanian_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-romanian-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> and the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-laurasydell_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-laurasydell-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-thehollywoodreporter_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thehollywoodreporter-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div avoid fake news online</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-57"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview_of_coverage">Overview of coverage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Overview of coverage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>One pan-European newspaper, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Local" title="The Local">The Local</a></i>, described the proliferation of fake news as a form of <a href="/wiki/Psychological_warfare" title="Psychological warfare">psychological warfare</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-concernoverbarrage_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-concernoverbarrage-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Some media analysts have seen it as a threat to democracy.<sup id="cite_ref-merkelwarns_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merkelwarns-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, the European Parliament\'s <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_Committee_on_Foreign_Affairs" title="European Parliament Committee on Foreign Affairs">Committee on Foreign Affairs</a> passed a resolution warning that the <a href="/wiki/Russian_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian government">Russian government</a> was using "pseudo-news agencies" and <a href="/wiki/Internet_troll" title="Internet troll">Internet trolls</a> as disinformation propaganda to weaken confidence in democratic values.<sup id="cite_ref-divideeurope_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-divideeurope-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:70news_fake_news_headline.png" class="image"><img alt="A screenshot of a fake news story, falsely claiming Donald Trump won the popular vote in the 2016 United States presidential election" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/5f/70news_fake_news_headline.png/300px-70news_fake_news_headline.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/5/5f/70news_fake_news_headline.png 1.5x" data-file-width="424" data-file-height="235" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:70news_fake_news_headline.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Screenshot of a fake news story, falsely stating <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_elections_in_which_the_winner_lost_the_popular_vote" class="mw-redirect" title="United States presidential elections in which the winner lost the popular vote">won the popular vote</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2016_United_States_presidential_election" title="2016 United States presidential election">2016 U.S. election</a><sup id="cite_ref-wapo14november2016_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wapo14november2016-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-politifact14november2016_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-politifact14november2016-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>In 2015, the <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Security_Service" title="Swedish Security Service">Swedish Security Service</a>, Sweden\'s national security agency, issued a report concluding Russia was using fake news to inflame "splits in society" through the proliferation of propaganda.<sup id="cite_ref-concernoverbarrage_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-concernoverbarrage-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Sweden\'s <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(Sweden)" title="Ministry of Defence (Sweden)">Ministry of Defence</a> tasked its <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Civil_Contingencies_Agency" title="Swedish Civil Contingencies Agency">Civil Contingencies Agency</a> with combating fake news from Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-concernoverbarrage_13-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-concernoverbarrage-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Fraudulent news affected politics in Indonesia and the Philippines, where there was simultaneously widespread usage of social media and limited resources to check the veracity of political claims.<sup id="cite_ref-MozurScott_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MozurScott-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> German Chancellor <a href="/wiki/Angela_Merkel" title="Angela Merkel">Angela Merkel</a> warned of the societal impact of "fake sites, bots, trolls".<sup id="cite_ref-merkelwarns_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merkelwarns-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Fraudulent articles spread through social media during the <a href="/wiki/2016_United_States_presidential_election" title="2016 United States presidential election">2016 U.S. presidential election</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-pbsrussianpropaganda_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbsrussianpropaganda-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-afprussianpropaganda_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afprussianpropaganda-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> and several officials within the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Intelligence_Community" title="United States Intelligence Community">U.S. Intelligence Community</a> said that Russia was engaged in spreading fake news.<sup id="cite_ref-watkins_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-watkins-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Computer_security" title="Computer security">Computer security</a> company <a href="/wiki/FireEye" title="FireEye">FireEye</a> concluded that Russia used social media to spread fake news stories<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>  as part of a <a href="/wiki/Cyberwarfare" title="Cyberwarfare">cyberwarfare</a> campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-strohm_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-strohm-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Google and <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a> banned fake sites from using <a href="/wiki/Online_advertising" title="Online advertising">online advertising</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-belfast_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-belfast-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-shanika_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shanika-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Facebook launched a partnership with <a href="/wiki/Fact-checking_websites" class="mw-redirect" title="Fact-checking websites">fact-checking websites</a> to flag fraudulent news and hoaxes; debunking organizations that joined the initiative included: <a href="/wiki/Snopes.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Snopes.com">Snopes.com</a>, <a href="/wiki/FactCheck.org" title="FactCheck.org">FactCheck.org</a>, and <a href="/wiki/PolitiFact" title="PolitiFact">PolitiFact</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-facebookisturning_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-facebookisturning-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> said a disregard for facts created a "dust cloud of nonsense".<sup id="cite_ref-zuckerbergsays_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zuckerbergsays-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Chief_of_the_Secret_Intelligence_Service" title="Chief of the Secret Intelligence Service">Chief of the Secret Intelligence Service</a> (MI6) <a href="/wiki/Alex_Younger" title="Alex Younger">Alex Younger</a> called fake news propaganda online dangerous for democratic nations.<sup id="cite_ref-mi6_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mi6-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Definition">Definition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Definition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:254px;max-width:254px"><div class="trow"><div class="theader">Examples of fake news websites</div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:252px;max-width:252px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:ABCnewscomco.png" class="image"><img alt="ABCnews.com.co" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/ABCnewscomco.png/250px-ABCnewscomco.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="87" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/ABCnewscomco.png/375px-ABCnewscomco.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/ABCnewscomco.png/500px-ABCnewscomco.png 2x" data-file-width="1416" data-file-height="493" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/ABCnews.com.co" title="ABCnews.com.co">ABCnews.com.co</a> - fake site creating <a href="/wiki/Hoax" title="Hoax">hoaxes</a> by using <a href="/wiki/Website_spoofing" title="Website spoofing">website spoofing</a></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:252px;max-width:252px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Denver_Guardian_logo.png" class="image"><img alt="Denver Guardian" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Denver_Guardian_logo.png/250px-Denver_Guardian_logo.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="41" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Denver_Guardian_logo.png/375px-Denver_Guardian_logo.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/53/Denver_Guardian_logo.png 2x" data-file-width="469" data-file-height="76" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Denver_Guardian" title="Denver Guardian">Denver Guardian</a></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:252px;max-width:252px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Everything_on_RealTrueNews_Was_A_LIE.jpg" class="image"><img alt="RealTrueNews" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Everything_on_RealTrueNews_Was_A_LIE.jpg/250px-Everything_on_RealTrueNews_Was_A_LIE.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="66" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Everything_on_RealTrueNews_Was_A_LIE.jpg/375px-Everything_on_RealTrueNews_Was_A_LIE.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Everything_on_RealTrueNews_Was_A_LIE.jpg/500px-Everything_on_RealTrueNews_Was_A_LIE.jpg 2x" data-file-width="760" data-file-height="201" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">RealTrueNews</div></div></div></div></div>\n<p><i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> has defined "fake news" on the internet as fictitious articles deliberately fabricated to deceive readers, generally with the goal of profiting through <a href="/wiki/Clickbait" title="Clickbait">clickbait</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-tavernise_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tavernise-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/PolitiFact" title="PolitiFact">PolitiFact</a> has described fake news as fabricated content designed to fool readers and subsequently made viral through the Internet to crowds that increase its dissemination.<sup id="cite_ref-kertscher_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kertscher-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Others have taken as constitutive the "systemic features inherent in the design of the sources and channels through which fake news proliferates", for example by playing to the audience\'s cognitive biases, heuristics, and partisan affiliation.<sup id="cite_ref-gelfert_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gelfert-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Some fake news websites use <a href="/wiki/Website_spoofing" title="Website spoofing">website spoofing</a>, structured to make visitors believe they are visiting trusted sources like <a href="/wiki/ABC_News" title="ABC News">ABC News</a> or <a href="/wiki/MSNBC" title="MSNBC">MSNBC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bengilbert_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bengilbert-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Fake news maintained a presence on the internet and in <a href="/wiki/Tabloid_journalism" title="Tabloid journalism">tabloid journalism</a> in the years prior to the <a href="/wiki/2016_United_States_presidential_election" title="2016 United States presidential election">2016 U.S. presidential election</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-tavernise_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tavernise-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Before the election campaign involving <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a>, fake news had not impacted the election process and subsequent events to such a high degree.<sup id="cite_ref-tavernise_35-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tavernise-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Subsequent to the 2016 election, the issue of fake news turned into a political weapon, with supporters of <a href="/wiki/Left-wing_politics" title="Left-wing politics">left-wing politics</a> saying that supporters of <a href="/wiki/Right-wing_politics" title="Right-wing politics">right-wing politics</a> spread false news, while the latter claimed that they were being "censored".<sup id="cite_ref-tavernise_35-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tavernise-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Due to these back-and-forth complaints, the definition of fake news as used for such polemics has become more vague.<sup id="cite_ref-tavernise_35-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tavernise-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-Internet_history">Pre-Internet history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Pre-Internet history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Journalistic_ethics" class="mw-redirect" title="Journalistic ethics">Unethical journalistic practices</a> existed in printed media for hundreds of years before the advent of the <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">Internet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-prihistory_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prihistory-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-politicohistory_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-politicohistory-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-scmphistory_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scmphistory-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Yellow_journalism" title="Yellow journalism">Yellow journalism</a>, reporting from a standard which is devoid of morals and professional ethics, was pervasive during the time period in history known as the <a href="/wiki/Gilded_Age" title="Gilded Age">Gilded Age</a>, and unethical journalists would engage in <a href="/wiki/Fraud" title="Fraud">fraud</a> by fabricating stories, interviews, and made-up names for scholars.<sup id="cite_ref-politicohistory_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-politicohistory-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-prihistory_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prihistory-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> During the 1890s, the spread of this unethical news sparked violence and conflicts.<sup id="cite_ref-prihistory_38-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prihistory-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Both <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Pulitzer" title="Joseph Pulitzer">Joseph Pulitzer</a> and <a href="/wiki/William_Randolph_Hearst" title="William Randolph Hearst">William Randolph Hearst</a> fomented yellow journalism in order to increase profits, which helped lead to misunderstandings which became partially responsible for the outset of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War">Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War</a> in 1898.<sup id="cite_ref-usatodayhistory_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usatodayhistory-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> J.B. Montgomery-M\xe2\x80\x99Govern wrote a column harshly critical of "fake news" in 1898, saying that what characterized "fake news" was sensationalism and "the publication of articles absolutely false, which tend to mislead an ignorant or unsuspecting public."<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Gleiwitz_incident" title="Gleiwitz incident">A radio broadcast from Gleiwitz</a> by German soldier Karl Homack, pretending to be a Polish invader who had captured the station, was taken at face value by other stations, in Germany and abroad, fueling <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a>\'s declaration of <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Poland" title="Invasion of Poland">war on Poland</a> the next day.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\nAccording to <i><a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a></i>, newspapers which have a history of commonly publishing fake news have included <i><a href="/wiki/Globe_(tabloid)" title="Globe (tabloid)">Globe</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Weekly_World_News" title="Weekly World News">Weekly World News</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/The_National_Enquirer" class="mw-redirect" title="The National Enquirer">The National Enquirer</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-usatodayhistory_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usatodayhistory-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Prominent_sources">Prominent sources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Prominent sources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_fake_news_websites" title="List of fake news websites">List of fake news websites</a></div>\n<p>Prominent <a href="/wiki/List_of_fake_news_websites" title="List of fake news websites">among fraudulent news sites</a> include false <a href="/wiki/Propaganda" title="Propaganda">propaganda</a> created by individuals in the countries of <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-russiadominates_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-russiadominates-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-divideeurope_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-divideeurope-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/North_Macedonia" title="North Macedonia">North Macedonia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-tynan_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tynan-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bengilbert_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bengilbert-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-romanian_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-romanian-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-laurasydell_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-laurasydell-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-thehollywoodreporter_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thehollywoodreporter-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="North_Macedonia">North Macedonia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: North Macedonia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Veles_panoram.JPG" class="image"><img alt="The town of Veles in North Macedonia" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Veles_panoram.JPG/220px-Veles_panoram.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Veles_panoram.JPG/330px-Veles_panoram.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Veles_panoram.JPG/440px-Veles_panoram.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Veles_panoram.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Fraudulent news stories during the 2016 U.S. election were traced to teenagers in <a href="/wiki/Veles,_North_Macedonia" title="Veles, North Macedonia">Veles, North Macedonia</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Much of the fake news during the <a href="/wiki/2016_United_States_presidential_election" title="2016 United States presidential election">2016 U.S. presidential election season</a> was traced to adolescents in Macedonia, now known as North Macedonia,<sup id="cite_ref-tynan_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tynan-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-condliffe_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-condliffe-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> specifically <a href="/wiki/Veles,_North_Macedonia" title="Veles, North Macedonia">Veles</a>. It is a town of 50,000 in the middle of the country, with high unemployment, where the average wage is $4,800.<sup id="cite_ref-smithbanic_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smithbanic-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> The income from fake news was characterized by <i>NBC News</i> as a <a href="/wiki/Gold_rush" title="Gold rush">gold rush</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-smithbanic_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smithbanic-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Adults supported this income, saying they were happy the youths were working.<sup id="cite_ref-apmacedonia_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-apmacedonia-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> The mayor of Veles, Slavcho Chadiev, said he was not bothered by their actions, as they were not against Macedonian law and their finances were taxable.<sup id="cite_ref-smithbanic_45-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smithbanic-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Chadiev said he was happy if deception from Veles influenced the results of the 2016 U.S. election in favor of Trump.<sup id="cite_ref-smithbanic_45-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smithbanic-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/BuzzFeed_News" title="BuzzFeed News">BuzzFeed News</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> separately investigated and found teenagers in Veles created over 100 sites spreading fake news stories supportive of <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-tynan_19-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tynan-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-howteens_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-howteens-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-daro_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-daro-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> The teenagers experimented with <a href="/wiki/Left-wing_politics" title="Left-wing politics">left slanted</a> fake stories about <a href="/wiki/Bernie_Sanders" title="Bernie Sanders">Bernie Sanders</a>, but found that pro-Trump fictions were more popular.<sup id="cite_ref-howteens_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-howteens-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Prior to the 2016 election the teenagers gained revenues from fake <a href="/wiki/Medical_advice" title="Medical advice">medical advice</a> sites.<sup id="cite_ref-pri_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pri-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> One youth named Alex stated, in an August 2016 interview with <i>The Guardian</i>, that this fraud would remain profitable regardless of who won the election.<sup id="cite_ref-tynan_19-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tynan-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Alex explained he plagiarized material for articles by <a href="/wiki/Cut,_copy,_and_paste" title="Cut, copy, and paste">copying and pasting</a> from other websites.<sup id="cite_ref-tynan_19-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tynan-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> This could net them thousands of dollars daily, but they averaged only a few thousand per month.<sup id="cite_ref-pri_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pri-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">Associated Press</a> (AP) interviewed an 18-year-old in Veles about his tactics.<sup id="cite_ref-apmacedonia_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-apmacedonia-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Google_Analytics" title="Google Analytics">Google Analytics</a> analysis of his traffic showed more than 650,000 views in one week.<sup id="cite_ref-apmacedonia_46-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-apmacedonia-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> He plagiarized pro-Trump stories from a <a href="/wiki/Right-wing_politics" title="Right-wing politics">right-wing</a> site called <i>The Political Insider</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-apmacedonia_46-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-apmacedonia-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> He said he did not care about politics, and published fake news to gain money and experience.<sup id="cite_ref-apmacedonia_46-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-apmacedonia-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> The AP used DomainTools to confirm the teenager was behind fake sites, and determined there were about 200 websites tracked to Veles focused on U.S. news, many of which mostly contained plagiarized legitimate news to create an appearance of credibility.<sup id="cite_ref-apmacedonia_46-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-apmacedonia-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/NBC_News" title="NBC News">NBC News</a></i> also interviewed an 18-year-old there.<sup id="cite_ref-smithbanic_45-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smithbanic-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Dmitri (a pseudonym) was one of the most profitable fake news operators in town, and said about 300 people in Veles wrote for fake sites.<sup id="cite_ref-smithbanic_45-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smithbanic-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Dmitri said he gained over $60,000 during the six months prior through doing this, more than both his parents\' earnings.<sup id="cite_ref-smithbanic_45-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smithbanic-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Dmitri said his main dupes were supporters of Trump.<sup id="cite_ref-smithbanic_45-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smithbanic-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> He said after the 2016 U.S. election he continued to earn significant amounts.<sup id="cite_ref-smithbanic_45-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smithbanic-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The 2020 U.S. election is their next project.<sup id="cite_ref-Y2020_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Y2020-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Romania">Romania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Romania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>"Ending the Fed", a popular purveyor of fraudulent reports, was run by a 24-year-old named Ovidiu Drobota out of <a href="/wiki/Oradea" title="Oradea">Oradea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a>, who boasted to <i><a href="/wiki/Inc._(magazine)" title="Inc. (magazine)">Inc. magazine</a></i> about being more popular than <a href="/wiki/Mainstream_media" title="Mainstream media">mainstream media</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-romanian_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-romanian-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Established in March 2016, "Ending the Fed" was responsible for a false story in August 2016 that incorrectly stated <a href="/wiki/Fox_News" title="Fox News">Fox News</a> had fired journalist <a href="/wiki/Megyn_Kelly" title="Megyn Kelly">Megyn Kelly</a>\xe2\x80\x94the story was briefly prominent on Facebook on its "Trending News" section.<sup id="cite_ref-romanian_21-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-romanian-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> "Ending the Fed" held four out of the 10 most popular fake articles on Facebook related to the 2016 U.S. election in the prior three months before the election itself.<sup id="cite_ref-romanian_21-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-romanian-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> The Facebook page for the website, called "End the Feed", had 350,000 "likes" in November 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-romanian_21-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-romanian-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> After being contacted by <i>Inc. magazine</i>, Drobota stated he was proud of the impact he had on the 2016 U.S. election in favor of his preferred candidate Donald Trump.<sup id="cite_ref-romanian_21-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-romanian-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Alexa_Internet" title="Alexa Internet">Alexa Internet</a>, "Ending the Fed" garnered approximately 3.4 million views over a 30-day-period in November 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-romanian_21-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-romanian-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Drobota stated the majority of incoming traffic is from Facebook.<sup id="cite_ref-romanian_21-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-romanian-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> He said his normal line of work before starting "Ending the Fed" included <a href="/wiki/Web_development" title="Web development">web development</a> and <a href="/wiki/Search_engine_optimization" title="Search engine optimization">search engine optimization</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-romanian_21-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-romanian-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Russia">Russia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Russia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Russian_propaganda" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian propaganda">Russian propaganda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cyberwarfare_by_Russia" title="Cyberwarfare by Russia">Cyberwarfare by Russia</a></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Internet_Research_Agency">Internet Research Agency</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Internet Research Agency">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Web_brigades" class="mw-redirect" title="Web brigades">Web brigades</a></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r997900035">.mw-parser-output .locmap .od{position:absolute}.mw-parser-output .locmap .id{position:absolute;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .locmap .l0{font-size:0;position:absolute}.mw-parser-output .locmap .pv{line-height:110%;position:absolute;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .locmap .pl{line-height:110%;position:absolute;top:-0.75em;text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .locmap .pr{line-height:110%;position:absolute;top:-0.75em;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .locmap .pv>div{display:inline;padding:1px}.mw-parser-output .locmap .pl>div{display:inline;padding:1px;float:right}.mw-parser-output .locmap .pr>div{display:inline;padding:1px;float:left}</style><div class="locmap noviewer thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px"><div style="position:relative;width:200px;border:1px solid lightgray"><a href="/wiki/File:Europe_blank_laea_location_map.svg" class="image" title="An aerial view of the Smolny Convent in Saint Petersburg"><img alt="An aerial view of the Smolny Convent in Saint Petersburg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Europe_blank_laea_location_map.svg/200px-Europe_blank_laea_location_map.svg.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="171" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Europe_blank_laea_location_map.svg/300px-Europe_blank_laea_location_map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Europe_blank_laea_location_map.svg/400px-Europe_blank_laea_location_map.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1401" data-file-height="1198" /></a><div class="od" style="top:29.789%;left:59.379%"><div class="id" style="left:-4px;top:-4px"><img alt="Saint Petersburg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Red_pog.svg/8px-Red_pog.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Saint Petersburg" width="8" height="8" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Red_pog.svg/12px-Red_pog.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Red_pog.svg/16px-Red_pog.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="64" data-file-height="64" /></div><div class="pr" style="font-size:91%;width:6em;left:5px"><div>Saint Petersburg</div></div></div></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Europe_blank_laea_location_map.svg" title="File:Europe blank laea location map.svg"> </a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Russian_propaganda" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian propaganda">Russian propaganda</a> "<a href="/wiki/Troll_farm" title="Troll farm">troll farm</a>" was traced back to <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">Saint Petersburg</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Beginning in fall 2014, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Yorker" title="The New Yorker">The New Yorker</a></i> writer <a href="/wiki/Adrian_Chen" title="Adrian Chen">Adrian Chen</a> performed a six-month investigation into Russian propaganda dissemination online by  the <a href="/wiki/Internet_Research_Agency" title="Internet Research Agency">Internet Research Agency</a> (IRA).<sup id="cite_ref-thenewyorkeradrianchen_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thenewyorkeradrianchen-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Yevgeny_Prigozhin" title="Yevgeny Prigozhin">Yevgeny Prigozhin</a> (Evgeny Prigozhin), a close associate of <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a>, was behind the operation which hired hundreds of individuals to work in <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">Saint Petersburg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-thenewyorkeradrianchen_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thenewyorkeradrianchen-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The organization became regarded as a "<a href="/wiki/Internet_troll" title="Internet troll">troll farm</a>", a term used to refer to propaganda efforts controlling many accounts online with the aim of artificially providing a semblance of a <a href="/wiki/Grassroots" title="Grassroots">grassroots</a> organization.<sup id="cite_ref-thenewyorkeradrianchen_18-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thenewyorkeradrianchen-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Chen reported that Internet trolling was used by the Russian government as a tactic largely after observing the social media organization of the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9313_Russian_protests" class="mw-redirect" title="2011\xe2\x80\x9313 Russian protests">2011 protests against Putin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-thenewyorkeradrianchen_18-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thenewyorkeradrianchen-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Union_response">European Union response</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: European Union response">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EP-Brussels-103.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Building of the European Union&#39;s Committee on Foreign Affairs" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/EP-Brussels-103.jpg/220px-EP-Brussels-103.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/EP-Brussels-103.jpg/330px-EP-Brussels-103.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/EP-Brussels-103.jpg/440px-EP-Brussels-103.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EP-Brussels-103.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> parliamentary <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_Committee_on_Foreign_Affairs" title="European Parliament Committee on Foreign Affairs">Committee on Foreign Affairs</a> passed a resolution in November 2016, condemning Russian "pseudo-news agencies" and <a href="/wiki/Internet_troll" title="Internet troll">Internet trolls</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2015, the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe</a> released an analysis critical of disinformation campaigns by <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> masked as news.<sup id="cite_ref-dwfakenews_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dwfakenews-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> This was intended to interfere with <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> relations with <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> after the removal of former Ukraine president <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Yanukovych" title="Viktor Yanukovych">Viktor Yanukovych</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-dwfakenews_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dwfakenews-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> According to <i><a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Welle" title="Deutsche Welle">Deutsche Welle</a></i>, similar tactics were used in the 2016 U.S. elections.<sup id="cite_ref-dwfakenews_51-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dwfakenews-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> created a taskforce to deal with Russian disinformation.<sup id="cite_ref-divideeurope_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-divideeurope-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dwfakenews_51-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dwfakenews-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The taskforce, <a href="/wiki/East_StratCom_Team" class="mw-redirect" title="East StratCom Team">East StratCom Team</a>, had 11 people including <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian speakers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-eumovestocounter_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eumovestocounter-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> In November 2016, the EU voted to increase the group\'s funding.<sup id="cite_ref-eumovestocounter_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eumovestocounter-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> In November 2016, the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_Committee_on_Foreign_Affairs" title="European Parliament Committee on Foreign Affairs">European Parliament Committee on Foreign Affairs</a> passed a resolution warning of the use by Russia of tools including: "pseudo-news agencies ... social media and internet trolls" as disinformation to weaken democratic values.<sup id="cite_ref-divideeurope_5-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-divideeurope-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The resolution requested EU analysts investigate, explaining member nations needed to be wary of disinformation.<sup id="cite_ref-divideeurope_5-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-divideeurope-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The resolution condemned Russian sources for publicizing "absolutely fake" news reports.<sup id="cite_ref-russiasfakenews_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-russiasfakenews-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> The tally on 23 November 2016 passed by a margin of 304 votes to 179.<sup id="cite_ref-russiasfakenews_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-russiasfakenews-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Counter-Disinformation_Team">Counter-Disinformation Team</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Counter-Disinformation Team">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<table Unreliable citations may be challenged or deleted.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">November 2020</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n    </div>\n</div><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State" title="United States Department of State">U.S. State Department</a> planned to use a unit called the Counter-Disinformation Team, formed with the intention of combating <a href="/wiki/Disinformation" title="Disinformation">disinformation</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Russian_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian government">Russian government</a>, and that it was disbanded in September 2015 after department heads missed the scope of propaganda before the <a href="/wiki/2016_United_States_presidential_election" title="2016 United States presidential election">2016 U.S. election</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-tomporter_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tomporter-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-propagandamachine_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-propagandamachine-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> The U.S. State Department put eight months into developing the unit before scrapping it.<sup id="cite_ref-tomporter_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tomporter-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> It would have been a reboot of the <a href="/wiki/Active_Measures_Working_Group" title="Active Measures Working Group">Active Measures Working Group</a> set up by <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_Ronald_Reagan" title="Presidency of Ronald Reagan">Reagan Administration</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-propagandamachine_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-propagandamachine-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kremlinsink_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kremlinsink-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> The Counter-Disinformation Team was set up under the <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_International_Information_Programs" title="Bureau of International Information Programs">Bureau of International Information Programs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-propagandamachine_56-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-propagandamachine-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kremlinsink_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kremlinsink-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Work began in 2014, with the intention to combat propaganda from Russian sources such as the <a href="/wiki/RT_(TV_network)" title="RT (TV network)">RT</a> network (formerly known as Russia Today).<sup id="cite_ref-propagandamachine_56-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-propagandamachine-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kremlinsink_57-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kremlinsink-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/United_States_Intelligence_Community" title="United States Intelligence Community">U.S. Intelligence</a> officials explained to former <a href="/wiki/National_Security_Agency" title="National Security Agency">National Security Agency</a> analyst and <a href="/wiki/Counterintelligence" title="Counterintelligence">counterintelligence</a> officer John R. Schindler that the <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_Barack_Obama" title="Presidency of Barack Obama">Obama Administration</a> decided to cancel the unit as they were afraid of antagonizing Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-propagandamachine_56-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-propagandamachine-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kremlinsink_57-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kremlinsink-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Under_Secretary_of_State_for_Public_Diplomacy_and_Public_Affairs" title="Under Secretary of State for Public Diplomacy and Public Affairs">U.S. Undersecretary of State for Public Diplomacy</a> <a href="/wiki/Richard_Stengel" title="Richard Stengel">Richard Stengel</a> was point person for the unit before it was canceled.<sup id="cite_ref-propagandamachine_56-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-propagandamachine-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kremlinsink_57-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kremlinsink-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Stengel previously wrote about disinformation by RT.<sup id="cite_ref-logiurato_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-logiurato-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-johnkerryrt_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-johnkerryrt-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-stengel_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stengel-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Internet_trolls_shift_focus_to_Trump">Internet trolls shift focus to Trump</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Internet trolls shift focus to Trump">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Adrian_Chen_at_IRL_Club_2016.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Adrian_Chen_at_IRL_Club_2016.JPG/170px-Adrian_Chen_at_IRL_Club_2016.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Adrian_Chen_at_IRL_Club_2016.JPG/255px-Adrian_Chen_at_IRL_Club_2016.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Adrian_Chen_at_IRL_Club_2016.JPG/340px-Adrian_Chen_at_IRL_Club_2016.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Adrian_Chen_at_IRL_Club_2016.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In December 2015 <a href="/wiki/Adrian_Chen" title="Adrian Chen">Adrian Chen</a> noticed pro-Russia accounts suddenly became supportive of Trump.</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Adrian_Chen" title="Adrian Chen">Adrian Chen</a> observed a pattern in December 2015 where pro-Russian accounts became supportive of 2016 U.S. presidential candidate Donald Trump.<sup id="cite_ref-russiadominates_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-russiadominates-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Andrew Weisburd and <a href="/wiki/Foreign_Policy_Research_Institute" title="Foreign Policy Research Institute">Foreign Policy Research Institute</a> fellow and senior fellow at the Center for Cyber and Homeland Security at <a href="/wiki/George_Washington_University" title="George Washington University">George Washington University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clint_Watts" title="Clint Watts">Clint Watts</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-behindrussias_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-behindrussias-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> wrote for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Beast" title="The Daily Beast">The Daily Beast</a></i> in August 2016 that Russian propaganda fabricated articles were popularized by social media.<sup id="cite_ref-russiadominates_3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-russiadominates-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Weisburd and Watts documented how disinformation spread from <a href="/wiki/Russia_Today" class="mw-redirect" title="Russia Today">Russia Today</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sputnik_News" class="mw-redirect" title="Sputnik News">Sputnik News</a>, "the two biggest Russian state-controlled media organizations publishing in English", to pro-Russian accounts on <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-russiadominates_3-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-russiadominates-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Citing research by Chen, Weisburd and Watts compared Russian tactics during the 2016 U.S. election to <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> strategies.<sup id="cite_ref-russiadominates_3-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-russiadominates-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> They referenced the 1992 <a href="/wiki/United_States_Information_Agency" title="United States Information Agency">United States Information Agency</a> report to Congress, which warned about Russian propaganda called <a href="/wiki/Active_measures" title="Active measures">active measures</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-russiadominates_3-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-russiadominates-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> They concluded social media made active measures easier.<sup id="cite_ref-russiadominates_3-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-russiadominates-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_International_Relations_Prague" title="Institute of International Relations Prague">Institute of International Relations Prague</a> senior fellow and scholar on Russian intelligence, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Galeotti" title="Mark Galeotti">Mark Galeotti</a>, agreed the Kremlin operations were a form of active measures.<sup id="cite_ref-watkins_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-watkins-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The most strident Internet promoters of Trump were not U.S. citizens but paid Russian propagandists. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> estimated  their number to be in the "low thousands" in November 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-invasionofthetroll_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-invasionofthetroll-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Weisburd and Watts collaborated with colleague J. M. Berger and published a follow-up to their <i>Daily Beast</i> article in online magazine <i>War on the Rocks</i>, titled: "Trolling for Trump: How Russia is Trying to Destroy Our Democracy".<sup id="cite_ref-behindrussias_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-behindrussias-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-witn_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-witn-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-trollingfortrump_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trollingfortrump-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> They researched 7,000 pro-Trump accounts over a <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1020198016">.mw-parser-output .frac{white-space:nowrap}.mw-parser-output .frac .num,.mw-parser-output .frac .den{font-size:80%;line-height:0;vertical-align:super}.mw-parser-output .frac .den{vertical-align:sub}.mw-parser-output .sr-only{border:0;clip:rect(0,0,0,0);height:1px;margin:-1px;overflow:hidden;padding:0;position:absolute;width:1px}</style><span class="frac" role="math">2<span class="sr-only">+</span><span class="num">1</span>&#8260;<span class="den">2</span></span>-year period.<sup id="cite_ref-witn_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-witn-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Their research detailed <a href="/wiki/Internet_troll" title="Internet troll">trolling techniques</a> to denigrate critics of Russian activities in Syria, and proliferate lies about Clinton\'s health.<sup id="cite_ref-witn_63-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-witn-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Watts said the propaganda targeted the <a href="/wiki/Alt-right" title="Alt-right">alt-right</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Right-wing_politics" title="Right-wing politics">right wing</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fascism" title="Fascism">fascist groups</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-behindrussias_61-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-behindrussias-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> After each presidential debate, thousands of Twitter bots used hashtag #Trumpwon to change perceptions.<sup id="cite_ref-moreworriedaboutmedia_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-moreworriedaboutmedia-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In November 2016 the <a href="/wiki/Foreign_Policy_Research_Institute" title="Foreign Policy Research Institute">Foreign Policy Research Institute</a><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup> stated Russian propaganda exacerbated criticism of Clinton and support for Trump.<sup id="cite_ref-pbsrussianpropaganda_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbsrussianpropaganda-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-afprussianpropaganda_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afprussianpropaganda-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The strategy involved social media, paid <a href="/wiki/Internet_troll" title="Internet troll">Internet trolls</a>, <a href="/wiki/Botnet" title="Botnet">botnets</a>, and websites in order to denigrate Clinton.<sup id="cite_ref-pbsrussianpropaganda_16-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbsrussianpropaganda-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-afprussianpropaganda_17-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afprussianpropaganda-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="U.S._intelligence_analysis">U.S. intelligence analysis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: U.S. intelligence analysis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dave_DeWalt,_CEO_and_Chairman_of_the_Board_from_acrofan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="David DeWalt, the chairman of computer security company FireEye" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Dave_DeWalt%2C_CEO_and_Chairman_of_the_Board_from_acrofan.jpg/170px-Dave_DeWalt%2C_CEO_and_Chairman_of_the_Board_from_acrofan.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Dave_DeWalt%2C_CEO_and_Chairman_of_the_Board_from_acrofan.jpg/255px-Dave_DeWalt%2C_CEO_and_Chairman_of_the_Board_from_acrofan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/5a/Dave_DeWalt%2C_CEO_and_Chairman_of_the_Board_from_acrofan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="302" data-file-height="355" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dave_DeWalt,_CEO_and_Chairman_of_the_Board_from_acrofan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/FireEye" title="FireEye">FireEye</a> chairman David DeWalt concluded the Russian operation during the 2016 election was a new development in <a href="/wiki/Cyberwarfare_by_Russia" title="Cyberwarfare by Russia">cyberwarfare by Russia</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Computer_security" title="Computer security">Computer security company</a> <a href="/wiki/FireEye" title="FireEye">FireEye</a> concluded Russia used social media as a weapon to influence the U.S. election.<sup id="cite_ref-strohm_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-strohm-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> FireEye Chairman David DeWalt said the 2016 operation was a new development in <a href="/wiki/Cyberwarfare_by_Russia" title="Cyberwarfare by Russia">cyberwarfare by Russia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-strohm_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-strohm-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> FireEye CEO Kevin Mandia stated Russian cyberwarfare changed after fall 2014, from covert to overt tactics with decreased <a href="/wiki/Operational_security" class="mw-redirect" title="Operational security">operational security</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-strohm_29-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-strohm-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bellingcat" title="Bellingcat">Bellingcat</a> analyst Aric Toler explained fact-checking only drew further attention to the fake news problem.<sup id="cite_ref-propagandatactics_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-propagandatactics-68">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/United_States_Intelligence_Community" title="United States Intelligence Community">U.S. Intelligence agencies</a> debated why Putin chose summer 2016 to escalate <a href="/wiki/Active_measures" title="Active measures">active measures</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-putinwinstheelection_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-putinwinstheelection-69">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Prior to the election, U.S. national security officials said they were anxious about Russia tampering with U.S. news.<sup id="cite_ref-moreworriedaboutmedia_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-moreworriedaboutmedia-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Director_of_National_Intelligence" title="Director of National Intelligence">Director of National Intelligence</a> <a href="/wiki/James_R._Clapper" class="mw-redirect" title="James R. Clapper">James R. Clapper</a> said after the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9313_Russian_protests" class="mw-redirect" title="2011\xe2\x80\x9313 Russian protests">2011\xe2\x80\x9313 Russian protests</a>, Putin lost <a href="/wiki/Self-confidence" class="mw-redirect" title="Self-confidence">self-confidence</a>, and responded with the propaganda operation.<sup id="cite_ref-putinwinstheelection_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-putinwinstheelection-69">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Former <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">CIA</a> officer Patrick Skinner said the goal was to spread uncertainty.<sup id="cite_ref-propagandatactics_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-propagandatactics-68">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/House_Permanent_Select_Committee_on_Intelligence" class="mw-redirect" title="House Permanent Select Committee on Intelligence">House Intelligence Committee</a> Ranking Member <a href="/wiki/Adam_Schiff" title="Adam Schiff">Adam Schiff</a> commented on Putin\'s aims, and said U.S. intelligence were concerned with Russian propaganda.<sup id="cite_ref-putinwinstheelection_69-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-putinwinstheelection-69">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Speaking about disinformation that appeared in <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>, Schiff said there was an increase of the same behavior in the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-putinwinstheelection_69-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-putinwinstheelection-69">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>U.S. intelligence officials stated in November 2016 they believed Russia engaged in spreading fake news,<sup id="cite_ref-watkins_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-watkins-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation" title="Federal Bureau of Investigation">FBI</a> released a statement saying they were investigating.<sup id="cite_ref-watkins_26-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-watkins-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-moreworriedaboutmedia_65-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-moreworriedaboutmedia-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Two U.S. intelligence officials each told <i>BuzzFeed News</i> they "believe Russia helped disseminate fake and propagandized news as part of a broader effort to influence and undermine the presidential election".<sup id="cite_ref-watkins_26-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-watkins-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The U.S. intelligence sources stated this involved "dissemination of completely fake news stories".<sup id="cite_ref-watkins_26-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-watkins-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> They told <i>BuzzFeed</i> the FBI investigation specifically focused on why "Russia had engaged in spreading false or misleading information".<sup id="cite_ref-watkins_26-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-watkins-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Fake_news_websites_in_the_United_States" title="Fake news websites in the United States">Fake news websites in the United States</a></div>\n<table class="box-Empty_section plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg" class="image"><img alt="[icon]" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="44" data-file-height="31" /></a></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span"><b>This section is empty.</b>  <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">May 2018</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="By_country">By country</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: By country">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Fake_news_by_country" class="mw-redirect" title="Fake news by country">Fake news by country</a></div>\n<p>Fake news has influenced political discourse in multiple countries, including <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-merkelwarns_11-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merkelwarns-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-MozurScott_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MozurScott-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-concernoverbarrage_13-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-concernoverbarrage-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-chinaonusfake_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chinaonusfake-70">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cadell_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cadell-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-maybetheinternet_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-maybetheinternet-72">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sheerafrenkel_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sheerafrenkel-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-russiadominates_3-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-russiadominates-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Austria">Austria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Austria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Politicians in Austria dealt with the impact of fake news and its spread on social media after the 2016 presidential campaign in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-austriaandgermany_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-austriaandgermany-73">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> In December 2016, a court in Austria issued an injunction on Facebook Europe, mandating it block negative postings related to <a href="/wiki/Eva_Glawischnig-Piesczek" title="Eva Glawischnig-Piesczek">Eva Glawischnig-Piesczek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Green_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Austrian Green Party">Austrian Green Party</a> Chairwoman.<sup id="cite_ref-austriaandgermany_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-austriaandgermany-73">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> According to <i>The Washington Post</i> the postings to Facebook about her "appeared to have been spread via a fake profile" and directed derogatory epithets towards the Austrian politician.<sup id="cite_ref-austriaandgermany_73-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-austriaandgermany-73">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> The derogatory postings were likely created by the identical fake profile that had previously been utilized to attack <a href="/wiki/Alexander_van_der_Bellen" class="mw-redirect" title="Alexander van der Bellen">Alexander van der Bellen</a>, who won the election for <a href="/wiki/President_of_Austria" title="President of Austria">President of Austria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-austriaandgermany_73-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-austriaandgermany-73">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Brazil">Brazil</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Brazil">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/WhatsApp#2018_elections_in_Brazil" title="WhatsApp">WhatsApp \xc2\xa7&#160;2018 elections in Brazil</a></div>\n<p>Brazil faced increasing influence from fake news after the <a href="/wiki/2014_Brazilian_general_election" title="2014 Brazilian general election">2014 re-election</a> of President <a href="/wiki/Dilma_Rousseff" title="Dilma Rousseff">Dilma Rousseff</a> and <a href="/wiki/Impeachment_of_Dilma_Rousseff" title="Impeachment of Dilma Rousseff">Rousseff\'s subsequent impeachment</a> in August 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-insidioustrend_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-insidioustrend-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> In the week surrounding one of the impeachment votes, 3 out of the 5 most-shared articles on Facebook in Brazil were fake.<sup id="cite_ref-insidioustrend_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-insidioustrend-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> In 2015, reporter Tai Nalon resigned from her position at Brazilian newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/Folha_de_S.Paulo" title="Folha de S.Paulo">Folha de S.Paulo</a></i> in order to start the first fact-checking website in Brazil, called Aos Fatos (To The Facts).<sup id="cite_ref-insidioustrend_74-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-insidioustrend-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Nalon told <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> there was a great deal of fake news, and hesitated to compare the problem to that experienced in the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-insidioustrend_74-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-insidioustrend-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Fake news online was brought to the attention of Canadian politicians in November 2016, as they debated helping assist local newspapers.<sup id="cite_ref-asfakenewsspreads_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-asfakenewsspreads-75">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Member of <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Canada" title="Parliament of Canada">Parliament</a> for <a href="/wiki/Vancouver_Centre" title="Vancouver Centre">Vancouver Centre</a> <a href="/wiki/Hedy_Fry" title="Hedy Fry">Hedy Fry</a> specifically discussed fake news as an example of ways in which publishers on the Internet are less accountable than print media.<sup id="cite_ref-asfakenewsspreads_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-asfakenewsspreads-75">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Discussion in parliament contrasted increase of fake news online with downsizing of Canadian newspapers and the impact for democracy in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-asfakenewsspreads_75-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-asfakenewsspreads-75">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Representatives from Facebook Canada attended the meeting and told members of Parliament they felt it was their duty to assist individuals gather data online.<sup id="cite_ref-asfakenewsspreads_75-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-asfakenewsspreads-75">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="China">China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Censorship_in_China" title="Censorship in China">Censorship in China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Internet_censorship_in_China" title="Internet censorship in China">Internet censorship in China</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_cyberwarfare" title="Chinese cyberwarfare">Chinese cyberwarfare</a></div>\n<p>Fake news during the 2016 U.S. election spread to China.<sup id="cite_ref-insidioustrend_74-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-insidioustrend-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Articles popularized within the United States were translated into Chinese and spread within China.<sup id="cite_ref-insidioustrend_74-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-insidioustrend-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_China" title="Government of China">government of China</a> used the growing problem of fake news as a rationale for increasing <a href="/wiki/Internet_censorship_in_China" title="Internet censorship in China">Internet censorship in China</a> in November 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-orlowski_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-orlowski-76">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> China then published an editorial in its <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Communist Party">Communist Party</a> newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/The_Global_Times" class="mw-redirect" title="The Global Times">The Global Times</a></i> called: "Western Media\'s Crusade Against Facebook", and criticized "unpredictable" political problems posed by freedoms enjoyed by users of <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-chinaonusfake_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chinaonusfake-70">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> China government leaders meeting in <a href="/wiki/Wuzhen" title="Wuzhen">Wuzhen</a> at the third <a href="/wiki/World_Internet_Conference" title="World Internet Conference">World Internet Conference</a> in November 2016 said fake news in the U.S. election justified adding more curbs to free and open use of the Internet.<sup id="cite_ref-cadell_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cadell-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> China Deputy Minister Ren Xianliang, official at the <a href="/wiki/Cyberspace_Administration_of_China" title="Cyberspace Administration of China">Cyberspace Administration of China</a>, said increasing online participation led to "harmful information" and fraud.<sup id="cite_ref-pascaline_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pascaline-77">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Kam Chow Wong, a former <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> law enforcement official and criminal justice professor at <a href="/wiki/Xavier_University" title="Xavier University">Xavier University</a>, praised attempts in the U.S. to patrol social media.<sup id="cite_ref-sodoeschina_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sodoeschina-78">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">The Wall Street Journal</a></i> noted China\'s themes of <a href="/wiki/Internet_censorship" title="Internet censorship">Internet censorship</a> became more relevant at the World Internet Conference due to the outgrowth of fake news.<sup id="cite_ref-chinapresses_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chinapresses-79">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Finland">Finland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section:
