Finland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Officials from 11 countries held a meeting in <a href="/wiki/Helsinki" title="Helsinki">Helsinki</a> in November 2016, in order to plan the formation of a center to combat disinformation cyber-warfare including spread of fake news on social media.<sup id="cite_ref-helsinkitohost_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-helsinkitohost-80">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> The center is planned to be located in Helsinki and include efforts from 10 countries with participation from Sweden, Germany, Finland, and the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-helsinkitohost_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-helsinkitohost-80">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Finland" title="Prime Minister of Finland">Prime Minister of Finland</a> <a href="/wiki/Juha_Sipil%C3%A4" title="Juha Sipil\xc3\xa4">Juha Sipil\xc3\xa4</a> planned to deal with the center in spring 2017 with a motion before the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Finland" title="Parliament of Finland">Parliament of Finland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-helsinkitohost_80-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-helsinkitohost-80">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Jori Arvonen, Deputy Secretary of State for EU Affairs, said cyberwarfare became an increased problem in 2016, and included hybrid cyber-warfare intrusions into Finland from Russia and <a href="/wiki/Islamic_State_of_Iraq_and_the_Levant" title="Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant">Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-helsinkitohost_80-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-helsinkitohost-80">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Arvonen cited examples including fake news online, disinformation, and the <a href="/wiki/Little_green_men_(Ukrainian_crisis)" title="Little green men (Ukrainian crisis)">little green men troops</a> during the Ukrainian crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-helsinkitohost_80-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-helsinkitohost-80">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="France">France</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: France">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>France saw an uptick in amounts of disinformation and propaganda, primarily in the midst of election cycles.<sup id="cite_ref-insidioustrend_74-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-insidioustrend-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Le_Monde" title="Le Monde">Le Monde</a></i> fact-checking division "Les d\xc3\xa9codeurs" was headed by Samuel Laurent, who told <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> in December 2016 the upcoming French presidential election campaign in spring 2017 would face problems from fake news.<sup id="cite_ref-insidioustrend_74-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-insidioustrend-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> The country faced controversy regarding fake websites providing false information about <a href="/wiki/Abortion" title="Abortion">abortion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-insidioustrend_74-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-insidioustrend-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> The government\'s lower parliamentary body moved forward with intentions to ban such fake sites.<sup id="cite_ref-insidioustrend_74-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-insidioustrend-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Laurence_Rossignol" title="Laurence Rossignol">Laurence Rossignol</a>, women\'s minister for France, informed parliament though the fake sites look neutral, in actuality their intentions were specifically targeted to give women fake information.<sup id="cite_ref-insidioustrend_74-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-insidioustrend-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> During the 10-year period preceding 2016, France was witness to an increase in popularity of <a href="/wiki/Far-right" class="mw-redirect" title="Far-right">far-right</a> alternative news sources called the <i>fachosphere</i> ("facho" referring to <a href="/wiki/Fascist" class="mw-redirect" title="Fascist">fascist</a>); known as the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Extreme_right_on_the_Internet&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Extreme right on the Internet (page does not exist)">extreme right on the Internet</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;&#91;<a href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extr%C3%AAme_droite_sur_Internet" class="extiw" title="fr:Extr\xc3\xaame droite sur Internet">fr</a>&#93;</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-insidioustrend_74-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-insidioustrend-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> According to sociologist Antoine Bevort, citing data from <a href="/wiki/Alexa_Internet" title="Alexa Internet">Alexa Internet</a> rankings, the most consulted political websites in France included <i><a href="/wiki/%C3%89galit%C3%A9_et_R%C3%A9conciliation" class="mw-redirect" title="\xc3\x89galit\xc3\xa9 et R\xc3\xa9conciliation">\xc3\x89galit\xc3\xa9 et R\xc3\xa9conciliation</a></i>, <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fran%C3%A7ois_Desouche&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Fran\xc3\xa7ois Desouche (page does not exist)">Fran\xc3\xa7ois Desouche</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;&#91;<a href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Desouche" class="extiw" title="fr:Fran\xc3\xa7ois Desouche">fr</a>&#93;</span></i>, and <i>Les Moutons Enrag\xc3\xa9s</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> These sites increased skepticism towards <a href="/wiki/Mainstream_media" title="Mainstream media">mainstream media</a> from both left and right perspectives.<sup id="cite_ref-insidioustrend_74-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-insidioustrend-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Germany">Germany</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Germany">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Chancellor_of_Germany" title="Chancellor of Germany">German Chancellor</a> <a href="/wiki/Angela_Merkel" title="Angela Merkel">Angela Merkel</a> lamented the problem of fraudulent news reports in a November 2016 speech, days after announcing her campaign for a fourth term as leader of her country.<sup id="cite_ref-merkelwarns_11-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merkelwarns-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> In a speech to the German parliament, Merkel was critical of such fake sites, saying they harmed political discussion.<sup id="cite_ref-merkelwarns_11-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merkelwarns-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Merkel called attention to the need of government to deal with <a href="/wiki/Internet_troll" title="Internet troll">Internet trolls</a>, bots, and fake news websites.<sup id="cite_ref-merkelwarns_11-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merkelwarns-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> She warned that such fraudulent news websites were a force increasing the power of <a href="/wiki/Populism" title="Populism">populist</a> extremism.<sup id="cite_ref-merkelwarns_11-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merkelwarns-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Merkel called fraudulent news a growing phenomenon that might need to be regulated in the future.<sup id="cite_ref-merkelwarns_11-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merkelwarns-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Germany\'s foreign intelligence agency <a href="/wiki/Federal_Intelligence_Service_(Germany)" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Intelligence Service (Germany)">Federal Intelligence Service</a> Chief, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bruno_Kahl_(BND_President)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bruno Kahl (BND President) (page does not exist)">Bruno Kahl</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;&#91;<a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bruno_Kahl" class="extiw" title="de:Bruno Kahl">de</a>&#93;</span>, warned of the potential for <a href="/wiki/Cyberattacks" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyberattacks">cyberattacks</a> by Russia in the <a href="/wiki/2017_German_federal_election" title="2017 German federal election">2017 German election</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-fisspychief_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fisspychief-83">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> He said the cyberattacks would take the form of the intentional spread of disinformation.<sup id="cite_ref-fisspychief_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fisspychief-83">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> Kahl said the goal is to increase chaos in political debates.<sup id="cite_ref-fisspychief_83-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fisspychief-83">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> Germany\'s domestic intelligence agency <a href="/wiki/Federal_Office_for_the_Protection_of_the_Constitution" title="Federal Office for the Protection of the Constitution">Federal Office for the Protection of the Constitution</a> Chief, <a href="/wiki/Hans-Georg_Maassen" class="mw-redirect" title="Hans-Georg Maassen">Hans-Georg Maassen</a>, said sabotage by Russian intelligence was a present threat to German <a href="/wiki/Information_security" title="Information security">information security</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-fisspychief_83-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fisspychief-83">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="India">India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: India">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Rasmus_Kleis_Nielsen" title="Rasmus Kleis Nielsen">Rasmus Kleis Nielsen</a>, director at <a href="/wiki/Reuters_Institute_for_the_Study_of_Journalism" title="Reuters Institute for the Study of Journalism">Reuters Institute for the Study of Journalism</a>, thinks that "the problems of disinformation in a society like India might be more sophisticated and more challenging than they are in the West".<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> The damage caused due to fake news on social media has increased due to the growth of the internet penetration in India, which has risen from 137 million internet users in 2012 to over 600&#160;million in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> India is the largest market for <a href="/wiki/WhatsApp" title="WhatsApp">WhatsApp</a>, with over 230 million users, and as a result one of the main platforms on which fake news is spread.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> One of the main problems is of receivers believing anything sent to them over social media due to lack of awareness.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Various initiatives and practices have been started and adopted to curb the spread and impact of fake news.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> Fake news is also spread through <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a>, <a href="/wiki/Whatsapp" class="mw-redirect" title="Whatsapp">Whatsapp</a><sup id="cite_ref-Quint_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Quint-90">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to a report by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i>, the Indian media research agency CMS stated that the cause of spread of fake news was that India "lacked (a) media policy for verification". Additionally, law enforcement officers have arrested reporters and journalists for "creating fictitious articles", especially when the articles were controversial.<sup id="cite_ref-Handbook2019_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Handbook2019-94">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In India, fake news has been spread by both the left and the right side of the political spectrum, though the right-wing is considered to be the dominant source of fake news. For example, a study published in <i><a href="/wiki/ThePrint" title="ThePrint">ThePrint</a></i> claimed that on Twitter, there were at least 17,000 accounts spreading fake news to favour the <a href="/wiki/BJP" class="mw-redirect" title="BJP">BJP</a>, while around 147 accounts were spreading fake news to favour the <a href="/wiki/Indian_National_Congress" title="Indian National Congress">Indian National Congress</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> Similarly, the IT Cell of the BJP has been accused of spreading fake news against the party\'s political opponents, religious minorities, and any campaigns against the party.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Quint_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Quint-90">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Prominent fake news-spreading websites and online resources include <a href="/wiki/OpIndia" title="OpIndia">OpIndia</a><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> and Postcard News.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Indonesia_and_Philippines">Indonesia and Philippines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Indonesia and Philippines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Fraudulent news has been particularly problematic in <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, where social media has an outsized political influence.<sup id="cite_ref-MozurScott_12-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MozurScott-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> According to media analysts, <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing countries</a> with new access to social media and democracy felt the fake news problem to a larger extent.<sup id="cite_ref-MozurScott_12-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MozurScott-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> In some developing countries, Facebook gives away smartphone data free of charge for Facebook and media sources, but at the same time does not provide the user with Internet access to fact-checking websites.<sup id="cite_ref-MozurScott_12-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MozurScott-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Iran">Iran</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Iran">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 8 October 2020, Bloomberg reported that 92 websites used by Iran to spread <a href="/wiki/Misinformation" title="Misinformation">misinformation</a> were seized by the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> government.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Italy">Italy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Italy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Laura_Boldrini_crop.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Laura_Boldrini_crop.jpg/170px-Laura_Boldrini_crop.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="204" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Laura_Boldrini_crop.jpg/255px-Laura_Boldrini_crop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Laura_Boldrini_crop.jpg/340px-Laura_Boldrini_crop.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1136" data-file-height="1360" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Laura_Boldrini_crop.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_the_Italian_Chamber_of_Deputies" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Presidents of the Italian Chamber of Deputies">President of the Italian Chamber of Deputies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Laura_Boldrini" title="Laura Boldrini">Laura Boldrini</a>, stated: "Fake news is a critical issue and we can\xe2\x80\x99t ignore it. We have to act now."<sup id="cite_ref-anxietyinitaly_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-anxietyinitaly-104">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>Between 1 October and 30 November 2016, ahead of the <a href="/wiki/2016_Italian_constitutional_referendum" title="2016 Italian constitutional referendum">Italian constitutional referendum</a>, five out of ten referendum-related stories with most social media participation were hoaxes or inaccurate.<sup id="cite_ref-kottasova_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kottasova-105">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-notizia_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-notizia-106">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Of the three stories with the most social media attention, two were fake.<sup id="cite_ref-notizia_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-notizia-106">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Italy" title="Prime Minister of Italy">Prime Minister of Italy</a> <a href="/wiki/Matteo_Renzi" title="Matteo Renzi">Matteo Renzi</a> met with U.S. President Obama and leaders of Europe at a meeting in <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> in November 2016, and spoke about the fake news problem.<sup id="cite_ref-anxietyinitaly_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-anxietyinitaly-104">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Renzi hosted discussions on <a href="/wiki/Facebook_Live" class="mw-redirect" title="Facebook Live">Facebook Live</a> in an effort to rebut falsities online.<sup id="cite_ref-kottasova_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kottasova-105">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> The influence became so heavy that a senior adviser to Renzi began a <a href="/wiki/Defamation" title="Defamation">defamation</a> complaint on an anonymous Twitter user who had used the screenname "Beatrice di Maio".<sup id="cite_ref-insidioustrend_74-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-insidioustrend-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Five_Star_Movement" title="Five Star Movement">Five Star Movement</a> (M5S), an Italian political party founded by <a href="/wiki/Beppe_Grillo" title="Beppe Grillo">Beppe Grillo</a>, managed fake news sites amplifying support for Russian news, propaganda, and inflamed <a href="/wiki/Conspiracy_theories" class="mw-redirect" title="Conspiracy theories">conspiracy theories</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-anxietyinitaly_104-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-anxietyinitaly-104">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-aristonandersonitaly_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aristonandersonitaly-107">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> The party\'s site <i>TzeTze</i> had 1.2 million Facebook fans and shared fake news and pieces supportive of Putin cited to Russia-owned sources including <i><a href="/wiki/Sputnik_News" class="mw-redirect" title="Sputnik News">Sputnik News</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-aristonandersonitaly_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aristonandersonitaly-107">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> <i>TzeTze</i> <a href="/wiki/Plagiarism" title="Plagiarism">plagiarized</a> the Russian sources, and copied article titles and content from <i>Sputnik</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-leadingeuropeinfake_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leadingeuropeinfake-108">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> TzeTze, another site critical of Renzi called <i>La Cosa</i>, and a blog by Grillo\xe2\x80\x94were managed by the company Casaleggio Associati which was started by Five Star Movement co-founder <a href="/wiki/Gianroberto_Casaleggio" title="Gianroberto Casaleggio">Gianroberto Casaleggio</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-aristonandersonitaly_107-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aristonandersonitaly-107">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> Casaleggio\'s son Davide Casaleggio owns and manages <i>TzeTze</i> and <i>La Cosa</i>, and medical advice website <i>La Fucina</i> which markets <a href="/wiki/Vaccine_controversies" class="mw-redirect" title="Vaccine controversies">anti-vaccine conspiracy theories</a> and <a href="/wiki/Panacea_(medicine)" title="Panacea (medicine)">medical cure-all methods</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-leadingeuropeinfake_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leadingeuropeinfake-108">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> Grillo\'s blog, Five Star Movement fake sites use the same <a href="/wiki/IP_address" title="IP address">IP addresses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Google_Analytics" title="Google Analytics">Google Analytics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Google_AdSense" title="Google AdSense">Google AdSense</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-leadingeuropeinfake_108-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leadingeuropeinfake-108">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Cyberwarfare against Renzi increased, and Italian newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/La_Stampa" title="La Stampa">La Stampa</a></i> brought attention to false stories by <i><a href="/wiki/Russia_Today" class="mw-redirect" title="Russia Today">Russia Today</a></i> which wrongly asserted a pro-Renzi rally in <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a> was actually an anti-Renzi rally.<sup id="cite_ref-insidioustrend_74-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-insidioustrend-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> In October 2016, the Five Star Movement disseminated a video from Kremlin-aligned <i>Russia Today</i> which falsely reported displaying thousands of individuals protesting the 4 December 2016 scheduled referendum in Italy\xe2\x80\x94when in fact the video that went on to 1.5 million views showed supporters of the referendum.<sup id="cite_ref-aristonandersonitaly_107-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aristonandersonitaly-107">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-leadingeuropeinfake_108-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leadingeuropeinfake-108">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_the_Italian_Chamber_of_Deputies" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Presidents of the Italian Chamber of Deputies">President of the Italian Chamber of Deputies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Laura_Boldrini" title="Laura Boldrini">Laura Boldrini</a>, stated: "Fake news is a critical issue and we can\xe2\x80\x99t ignore it. We have to act now."<sup id="cite_ref-anxietyinitaly_104-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-anxietyinitaly-104">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Boldrini met on 30 November 2016 with vice president of public policy in Europe for Facebook Richard Allan to voice concerns about fake news.<sup id="cite_ref-anxietyinitaly_104-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-anxietyinitaly-104">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> She said Facebook needed to admit they were a media company.<sup id="cite_ref-anxietyinitaly_104-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-anxietyinitaly-104">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mexico">Mexico</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Mexico">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Elections in Mexico are always rigged by the misinformation that is let out in the public. This is true for any political party, whether they are democratic or authoritarian. Due to the false information that easily influences voters in Mexico, it can threaten that state of the country because actions that are taken by misinformed citizens. In Mexico, fake exit polls have been moving within digital media outlets. What this means is that citizens are not receiving real data on what is happening in their elections.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Moldova">Moldova</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Moldova">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Amid the 2018 local elections in Moldova a doctored video with mistranslated subtitles purported to show that the a pro-Europe party candidate for mayor of Chisinau (pop. 685,900), the capital of Moldova had proposed to lease the city of Chisinau to the UAE for 50 years.<sup id="cite_ref-dfrlab_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dfrlab-110">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> The video was watched more than 300,000 times on Facebook and almost 250,000 times on the Russian social network site OK.ru, which is popular among Moldova\'s Russian-speaking population.<sup id="cite_ref-dfrlab_110-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dfrlab-110">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Myanmar">Myanmar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Myanmar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims_in_Myanmar" title="Persecution of Muslims in Myanmar">Persecution of Muslims in Myanmar</a></div>\n<p>In 2015, fake stories using unrelated photographs and fraudulent captions were shared online in support of the <a href="/wiki/Rohingya" class="mw-redirect" title="Rohingya">Rohingya</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Fake news negatively affected individuals in <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a>, leading to a rise in <a href="/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims_in_Myanmar" title="Persecution of Muslims in Myanmar">violence against Muslims in the country</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-maybetheinternet_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-maybetheinternet-72">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sheerafrenkel_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sheerafrenkel-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Online participation surged from one percent to 20 percent of Myanmar\'s total populace from 2014 to 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-maybetheinternet_72-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-maybetheinternet-72">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sheerafrenkel_15-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sheerafrenkel-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Fake stories from Facebook were reprinted in paper periodicals called <i>Facebook</i> and <i>The Internet</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-sheerafrenkel_15-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sheerafrenkel-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> False reporting related to practitioners of Islam in the country was directly correlated with increased attacks on <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Myanmar" title="Islam in Myanmar">people of the religion in Myanmar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-maybetheinternet_72-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-maybetheinternet-72">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sheerafrenkel_15-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sheerafrenkel-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Fake news fictitiously stated believers in Islam acted out in violence at Buddhist locations.<sup id="cite_ref-maybetheinternet_72-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-maybetheinternet-72">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sheerafrenkel_15-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sheerafrenkel-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> <i>BuzzFeed News</i> documented a direct relationship between the fake news and violence against Muslim people.<sup id="cite_ref-maybetheinternet_72-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-maybetheinternet-72">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sheerafrenkel_15-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sheerafrenkel-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> It noted countries that were relatively newer to Internet exposure were more vulnerable to the problems of fake news and fraud.<sup id="cite_ref-sheerafrenkel_15-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sheerafrenkel-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pakistan">Pakistan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Pakistan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Khawaja_Muhammad_Asif" title="Khawaja Muhammad Asif">Khawaja Muhammad Asif</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pakistan_Ministry_of_Defence" class="mw-redirect" title="Pakistan Ministry of Defence">Minister of Defence</a> of <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, threatened to nuke <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> on <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> after a false story claiming that <a href="/wiki/Avigdor_Lieberman" title="Avigdor Lieberman">Avigdor Lieberman</a>, the Israeli <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defense_(Israel)" title="Ministry of Defense (Israel)">Ministry of Defense</a>, said "If Pakistan send ground troops into Syria on any pretext, we will destroy this country with a nuclear attack."<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Poland">Poland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Poland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2016 Polish historian <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jerzy_Targalski&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jerzy Targalski (page does not exist)">Jerzy Targalski</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;&#91;<a href="https://pl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerzy_Targalski" class="extiw" title="pl:Jerzy Targalski">pl</a>&#93;</span> noted fake news websites had infiltrated Poland through <a href="/wiki/Anti-establishment" title="Anti-establishment">anti-establishment</a> and <a href="/wiki/Right-wing" class="mw-redirect" title="Right-wing">right-wing</a> focused sources that copied content from <i><a href="/wiki/Russia_Today" class="mw-redirect" title="Russia Today">Russia Today</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-disinformationexperts_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-disinformationexperts-114">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Targalski observed there existed about 20 specific fake news websites in Poland which spread Russian disinformation in the form of fake news.<sup id="cite_ref-disinformationexperts_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-disinformationexperts-114">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> One example cited was the false claim that <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> had claimed that the Polish city of <a href="/wiki/Przemy%C5%9Bl" title="Przemy\xc5\x9bl">Przemy\xc5\x9bl</a> was occupied by Poland.<sup id="cite_ref-disinformationexperts_114-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-disinformationexperts-114">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> In 2020 fake news websites related to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a> have been identified and officially labelled as such by the Polish Ministry of Health.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sweden">Sweden</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Sweden">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Security_Service" title="Swedish Security Service">Swedish Security Service</a> issued a report in 2015 identifying propaganda from Russia infiltrating Sweden with the objective to amplify pro-Russian propaganda and inflame societal conflicts.<sup id="cite_ref-concernoverbarrage_13-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-concernoverbarrage-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Civil_Contingencies_Agency" title="Swedish Civil Contingencies Agency">Swedish Civil Contingencies Agency</a> (MSB), part of the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(Sweden)" title="Ministry of Defence (Sweden)">Ministry of Defence of Sweden</a>, identified fake news reports targeting <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> in 2016 which originated from Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-concernoverbarrage_13-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-concernoverbarrage-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Swedish Civil Contingencies Agency official Mikael Tofvesson stated a pattern emerged where views critical of Sweden were constantly repeated.<sup id="cite_ref-concernoverbarrage_13-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-concernoverbarrage-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The MSB identified <i><a href="/wiki/Russia_Today" class="mw-redirect" title="Russia Today">Russia Today</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Sputnik_News" class="mw-redirect" title="Sputnik News">Sputnik News</a></i> as significant fake news purveyors.<sup id="cite_ref-concernoverbarrage_13-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-concernoverbarrage-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> As a result of growth in this propaganda in Sweden, the MSB planned to hire six additional security officials to fight back against the campaign of fraudulent information.<sup id="cite_ref-concernoverbarrage_13-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-concernoverbarrage-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Taiwan">Taiwan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Taiwan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In a report in December 2015 by <i><a href="/wiki/The_China_Post" title="The China Post">The China Post</a></i>, a fake video shared online showed people a light show purportedly made at the <a href="/wiki/Shihmen_Reservoir" class="mw-redirect" title="Shihmen Reservoir">Shihmen Reservoir</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-lightshow_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lightshow-116">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> The Northern Region Water Resources Office confirmed there was no light show at the reservoir and the event had been fabricated.<sup id="cite_ref-lightshow_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lightshow-116">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> The fraud led to an increase in tourist visits to the actual attraction.<sup id="cite_ref-lightshow_116-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lightshow-116">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ukraine">Ukraine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Ukraine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><i><a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Welle" title="Deutsche Welle">Deutsche Welle</a></i> interviewed the founder of Stopfake.org in 2014 about the website\'s efforts to debunk fake news in Ukraine, including <a href="/wiki/Media_portrayal_of_the_Ukrainian_crisis" title="Media portrayal of the Ukrainian crisis">media portrayal of the Ukrainian crisis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-chimbelu_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chimbelu-117">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Co-founder Margot Gontar began the site in March 2014, and it was aided by volunteers.<sup id="cite_ref-chimbelu_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chimbelu-117">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> In 2014, <i>Deutsche Welle</i> awarded the fact-checker website with the People\'s Choice Award for Russian in its ceremony <a href="/wiki/The_BOBs_(weblog_award)" title="The BOBs (weblog award)">The BOBs</a>, recognizing excellence in advocacy on the Internet.<sup id="cite_ref-chimbelu_117-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chimbelu-117">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Gontar highlighted an example debunked by the website, where a fictitious "Doctor Rozovskii" supposedly told <i>The Guardian</i> pro-Ukraine individuals refused to allow him to tend to injured in fighting with Russian supporters in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-chimbelu_117-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chimbelu-117">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Stopfake.org exposed the event was fabricated\xe2\x80\x94there actually was no individual named "Doctor Rozovskii", and found the Facebook photo distributed with the incident was of a different individual from Russia with a separate identity.<sup id="cite_ref-chimbelu_117-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chimbelu-117">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Former Ukraine president <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Yanukovych" title="Viktor Yanukovych">Viktor Yanukovych</a>\'s ouster from power created instability, and in 2015 the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe</a> concluded Russian disinformation campaigns used fake news to disrupt relations between Europe and Ukraine.<sup id="cite_ref-dwfakenews_51-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dwfakenews-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Russian-financed news spread disinformation after the conflict in Ukraine motivated the European Union to found the <a href="/wiki/European_External_Action_Service" title="European External Action Service">European External Action Service</a> specialist task force to counter the propaganda.<sup id="cite_ref-dwfakenews_51-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dwfakenews-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Fake_news_by_country#United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Fake news by country">Fake news by country \xc2\xa7&#160;United Kingdom</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Russian_interference_in_the_2016_Brexit_referendum" title="Russian interference in the 2016 Brexit referendum">Russian interference in the 2016 Brexit referendum</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a> MP <a href="/wiki/Michael_Dugher" title="Michael Dugher">Michael Dugher</a> was assigned by <a href="/wiki/Deputy_Leader_of_the_Labour_Party_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="Deputy Leader of the Labour Party (UK)">Deputy Leader of the Labour Party</a> <a href="/wiki/Tom_Watson_(Labour_politician)" title="Tom Watson (Labour politician)">Tom Watson</a> in November 2016 to investigate the impact of fake news spread through social media.<sup id="cite_ref-labourispromising_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-labourispromising-118">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> Watson said they would work with Twitter and Facebook to root out clear-cut circumstances of "downright lies".<sup id="cite_ref-labourispromising_118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-labourispromising-118">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> Watson wrote an article for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">The Independent</a></i> where he suggested methods to respond to fake news, including Internet-based societies which fact-check in a manner modeled after <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia" title="Wikipedia">Wikipedia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-thomaswatson_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thomaswatson-119">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Department_for_Culture,_Media_and_Sport" class="mw-redirect" title="Department for Culture, Media and Sport">Minister for Culture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Hancock" class="mw-redirect" title="Matthew Hancock">Matthew Hancock</a>, stated the British government would investigate the impact of fake news and its pervasiveness on social media websites.<sup id="cite_ref-thegovernmentsays_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thegovernmentsays-120">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> Watson stated he welcomed the investigation into fake news by the government.<sup id="cite_ref-thegovernmentsays_120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thegovernmentsays-120">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> On 8 December 2016, <a href="/wiki/Chief_of_the_Secret_Intelligence_Service" title="Chief of the Secret Intelligence Service">Chief of the Secret Intelligence Service</a> (MI6) <a href="/wiki/Alex_Younger" title="Alex Younger">Alex Younger</a> delivered a speech to journalists at the <a href="/wiki/SIS_Building" title="SIS Building">MI6 headquarters</a> where he called fake news and propaganda damaging to democracy.<sup id="cite_ref-mi6_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mi6-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Younger said the mission of MI6 was to combat propaganda and fake news in order to deliver to his government a strategic advantage in the <a href="/wiki/Information_warfare" title="Information warfare">information warfare</a> arena, and assist other nations including European countries.<sup id="cite_ref-mi6_34-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mi6-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> He called such methods of fake news propaganda online as a "fundamental threat to our sovereignty".<sup id="cite_ref-mi6_34-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mi6-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Younger said all nations that hold democratic values should feel the same worry over fake news.<sup id="cite_ref-mi6_34-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mi6-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States_2">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Fake_news_websites_in_the_United_States" title="Fake news websites in the United States">Fake news websites in the United States</a></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2016_election_cycle">2016 election cycle</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: 2016 election cycle">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/2016_United_States_election_interference_by_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="2016 United States election interference by Russia">2016 United States election interference by Russia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Barack_Obama_in_October_2016.jpg" class="image"><img alt="U.S. President Barack Obama" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Barack_Obama_in_October_2016.jpg/170px-Barack_Obama_in_October_2016.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="258" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Barack_Obama_in_October_2016.jpg/255px-Barack_Obama_in_October_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Barack_Obama_in_October_2016.jpg/340px-Barack_Obama_in_October_2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="629" data-file-height="955" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Barack_Obama_in_October_2016.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> said, "If we can\'t discriminate between serious arguments and propaganda, then we have problems."<sup id="cite_ref-jaketapper_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jaketapper-121">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HarrisEddy_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HarrisEddy-122">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>Fraudulent stories during the <a href="/wiki/2016_United_States_presidential_election" title="2016 United States presidential election">2016 U.S. presidential election</a> popularized on Facebook included a <a href="/wiki/Viral_phenomenon" title="Viral phenomenon">viral post</a> that <a href="/wiki/Pope_Francis" title="Pope Francis">Pope Francis</a> had endorsed <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a>, and another that actor <a href="/wiki/Denzel_Washington" title="Denzel Washington">Denzel Washington</a> "backs Trump in the most epic way possible".<sup id="cite_ref-alyssanewcomb_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alyssanewcomb-123">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-didthepope_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-didthepope-124">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> Donald Trump\'s son and campaign surrogate <a href="/wiki/Eric_Trump" title="Eric Trump">Eric Trump</a>, top national security adviser <a href="/wiki/Michael_T._Flynn" class="mw-redirect" title="Michael T. Flynn">Michael T. Flynn</a>, and then-campaign managers <a href="/wiki/Kellyanne_Conway" title="Kellyanne Conway">Kellyanne Conway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Corey_Lewandowski" title="Corey Lewandowski">Corey Lewandowski</a> shared fake news stories during the campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-jaketapper_121-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jaketapper-121">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fakenewswriter_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fakenewswriter-125">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mostgullible_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mostgullible-126">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bothtweetobviously_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bothtweetobviously-127">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Misuse_of_the_term">Misuse of the term</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Misuse of the term">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>After the 2016 election, Republican politicians and conservative media began to <a href="/wiki/Reappropriation" title="Reappropriation">appropriate</a> the term by using it to describe any news they see as hostile to their agenda, according to <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, which cited <a href="/wiki/Breitbart_News" title="Breitbart News">Breitbart News</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rush_Limbaugh" title="Rush Limbaugh">Rush Limbaugh</a> and supporters of <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> as dismissing true mainstream news reports, and any news they do not like as "fake news".<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_25_December_2016_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_25_December_2016-128">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="U.S._response_to_Russia_in_Syria">U.S. response to Russia in Syria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: U.S. response to Russia in Syria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The Russian state-operated newswire <a href="/wiki/RIA_Novosti" title="RIA Novosti">RIA Novosti</a>, known as Sputnik International, reported fake news and fabricated statements by <a href="/wiki/White_House_Press_Secretary" title="White House Press Secretary">White House Press Secretary</a> <a href="/wiki/Josh_Earnest" title="Josh Earnest">Josh Earnest</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-fakenewsinrussia_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fakenewsinrussia-129">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> RIA Novosti falsely reported on 7 December 2016 that Earnest stated sanctions for Russia were on the table related to Syria.<sup id="cite_ref-fakenewsinrussia_129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fakenewsinrussia-129">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> RIA Novosti falsely quoted Earnest as saying: "There are a number of things that are to be considered, including some of the financial sanctions that the United States can administer in coordination with our allies. I would definitely not rule that out."<sup id="cite_ref-fakenewsinrussia_129-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fakenewsinrussia-129">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> However, the word "sanctions" was never used by the Press Secretary.<sup id="cite_ref-fakenewsinrussia_129-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fakenewsinrussia-129">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> Russia was discussed in eight instances during the press conference, but never about sanctions.<sup id="cite_ref-fakenewsinrussia_129-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fakenewsinrussia-129">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> The press conference focused solely on Russian air raids in Syria towards rebels fighting <a href="/wiki/President_of_Syria" title="President of Syria">President of Syria</a> <a href="/wiki/Bashar_al-Assad" title="Bashar al-Assad">Bashar al-Assad</a> in <a href="/wiki/Aleppo" title="Aleppo">Aleppo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-fakenewsinrussia_129-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fakenewsinrussia-129">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Legislative_and_executive_responses">Legislative and executive responses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Legislative and executive responses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Members of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate_Select_Committee_on_Intelligence" title="United States Senate Select Committee on Intelligence">U.S. Senate Intelligence Committee</a> traveled to Ukraine and Poland in March 2016 and heard about Russian operations to influence internal Ukrainian matters.<sup id="cite_ref-angusking_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-angusking-130">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> Senator <a href="/wiki/Angus_King" title="Angus King">Angus King</a> recalled they were informed about Russia "planting fake news stories" during elections.<sup id="cite_ref-angusking_130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-angusking-130">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> On 30 November 2016 seven members of the Senate Intelligence Committee asked President Obama to publicize information on Russia\'s role in spreading disinformation in the U.S. election.<sup id="cite_ref-angusking_130-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-angusking-130">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-afpobamaorders_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afpobamaorders-131">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kingamong_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kingamong-132">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> On 30 November 2016, legislators approved a measure within the <a href="/wiki/National_Defense_Authorization_Act" title="National Defense Authorization Act">National Defense Authorization Act</a> to finance the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State" title="United States Department of State">U.S. State Department</a> to act against foreign propaganda.<sup id="cite_ref-combatpropaganda_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-combatpropaganda-133">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-representativesbacks_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-representativesbacks-134">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> The initiative was developed through a <a href="/wiki/Bipartisan" class="mw-redirect" title="Bipartisan">bipartisan</a> bill, the <a href="/wiki/Countering_Foreign_Propaganda_and_Disinformation_Act" title="Countering Foreign Propaganda and Disinformation Act">Countering Foreign Propaganda and Disinformation Act</a>, written by U.S. Senators Republican <a href="/wiki/Rob_Portman" title="Rob Portman">Rob Portman</a> and Democrat <a href="/wiki/Chris_Murphy_(Connecticut_politician)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chris Murphy (Connecticut politician)">Chris Murphy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-combatpropaganda_133-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-combatpropaganda-133">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> Republican U.S. Senators stated they planned to hold hearings and investigate Russian influence on the 2016 U.S. elections.<sup id="cite_ref-republicansready_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-republicansready-135">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> By doing so they went against the preference of incoming Republican President-elect Donald Trump, who downplayed any potential Russian meddling in the election.<sup id="cite_ref-republicansready_135-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-republicansready-135">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate_Committee_on_Armed_Services" title="United States Senate Committee on Armed Services">Senate Armed Services Committee</a> Chairman <a href="/wiki/John_McCain" title="John McCain">John McCain</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate_Select_Committee_on_Intelligence" title="United States Senate Select Committee on Intelligence">Senate Intelligence Committee</a> Chairman <a href="/wiki/Richard_Burr" title="Richard Burr">Richard Burr</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate_Committee_on_Foreign_Relations" title="United States Senate Committee on Foreign Relations">U.S. Senate Foreign Relations Committee</a> Chairman <a href="/wiki/Bob_Corker" title="Bob Corker">Bob Corker</a>, and Senator <a href="/wiki/Lindsey_Graham" title="Lindsey Graham">Lindsey Graham</a> all planned investigations in the <a href="/wiki/115th_United_States_Congress" title="115th United States Congress">115th U.S. Congress session</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-republicansready_135-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-republicansready-135">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">U.S. President</a> <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> commented on fake news online in a speech the day before <a href="/wiki/Election_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="Election Day">Election Day</a> in 2016, saying social media spread lies and created a "dust cloud of nonsense".<sup id="cite_ref-zuckerbergsays_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zuckerbergsays-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> Obama commented again on the problem after the election: "if we can\'t discriminate between serious arguments and propaganda, then we have problems."<sup id="cite_ref-jaketapper_121-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jaketapper-121">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HarrisEddy_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HarrisEddy-122">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> On 9 December 2016, President Obama ordered <a href="/wiki/United_States_Intelligence_Community" title="United States Intelligence Community">U.S. Intelligence Community</a> to conduct a complete review of the Russian propaganda operation.<sup id="cite_ref-ciareportrussiatrump_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ciareportrussiatrump-137">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> In his year-end press conference on 16 December 2016, President Obama criticized a hyper-partisan atmosphere for enabling the proliferation of fake news.<sup id="cite_ref-americascore_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-americascore-138">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Conspiracy_theories_and_2016_pizzeria_attack">Conspiracy theories and 2016 pizzeria attack</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Conspiracy theories and 2016 pizzeria attack">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In November 2016, fake news sites and Internet forums falsely implicated the restaurant <a href="/wiki/Comet_Ping_Pong" title="Comet Ping Pong">Comet Ping Pong</a> and <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic Party</a> figures as part of a fictitious <a href="/wiki/Child_trafficking" class="mw-redirect" title="Child trafficking">child trafficking</a> ring, which was dubbed "<a href="/wiki/Pizzagate_conspiracy_theory" title="Pizzagate conspiracy theory">Pizzagate</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-bbc-pizzagate_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-pizzagate-139">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> The rumor was widely debunked by sources such as the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Police_Department_of_the_District_of_Columbia" title="Metropolitan Police Department of the District of Columbia">Metropolitan Police Department of the District of Columbia</a>, fact-checking website <a href="/wiki/Snopes.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Snopes.com">Snopes.com</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, and <a href="/wiki/Fox_News" title="Fox News">Fox News</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DCGunman_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DCGunman-142">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Fox_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fox-143">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> The restaurant\'s owners were harassed and threatened, and increased their security.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc-pizzagate_139-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-pizzagate-139">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> On 4 December 2016, an individual from <a href="/wiki/Salisbury,_North_Carolina" title="Salisbury, North Carolina">Salisbury, North Carolina</a>, walked into the restaurant to "self-investigate" this conspiracy theory. He brought a <a href="/wiki/Semi-automatic_rifle" title="Semi-automatic rifle">semi-automatic rifle</a>, and fired shots before being arrested; no one was injured.<sup id="cite_ref-DCGunman_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DCGunman-142">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> The suspect told police that he planned to "self-investigate" the conspiracy theory,<sup id="cite_ref-DCGunman_142-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DCGunman-142">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> and was charged with assault with a dangerous weapon, carrying a pistol without a license, unlawful discharge of a firearm, and carrying a rifle or shotgun outside the home or business.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> After the incident, future <a href="/wiki/National_Security_Advisor_(United_States)" title="National Security Advisor (United States)">National Security Advisor</a> <a href="/wiki/Michael_T._Flynn" class="mw-redirect" title="Michael T. Flynn">Michael T. Flynn</a> and his son Michael G. Flynn were criticized by many reporters for spreading the rumors.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> Two days after the shooting, Trump fired Michael G. Flynn from his transition team in connection with Flynn\'s Twitter posting of fake news.<sup id="cite_ref-trumpfires_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trumpfires-151">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-forcedout_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forcedout-152">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> Days after the attack, <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a> spoke out on the dangers of fake news in a tribute speech to retiring Senator <a href="/wiki/Harry_Reid" title="Harry Reid">Harry Reid</a> at the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Capitol" title="United States Capitol">U.S. Capitol</a>, and called the problem an <a href="/wiki/Epidemic" title="Epidemic">epidemic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-clintonattacksfake_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-clintonattacksfake-153">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-clintonwarnsepidemic_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-clintonwarnsepidemic-154">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2018_Midterm_Elections">2018 Midterm Elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: 2018 Midterm Elections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>To track junk news shared on Facebook during the 2018 midterm elections, the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://newsaggregator.oii.ox.ac.uk/">Junk News Aggregator</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20210127212508/https://newsaggregator.oii.ox.ac.uk/">Archived</a> 2021-01-27 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a> was launched by the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://comprop.oii.ox.ac.uk/">Computational Propaganda Project</a> of the Oxford Internet Institute, University of Oxford. This Aggregator is a public platform, offering three interactive tools for tracking in near real-time public posts shared on Facebook by junk news sources, showing the content and the user engagement numbers that these posts have received.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Response">Response</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Response">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fact-checking_websites_and_journalists">Fact-checking websites and journalists</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Fact-checking websites and journalists">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/FactCheck.org" title="FactCheck.org">FactCheck.org</a>, <a href="/wiki/PolitiFact.com" class="mw-redirect" title="PolitiFact.com">PolitiFact.com</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Snopes.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Snopes.com">Snopes.com</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:PolitiFact_logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="Logo of PolitiFact" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/PolitiFact_logo.svg/350px-PolitiFact_logo.svg.png" decoding="async" width="350" height="60" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/PolitiFact_logo.svg/525px-PolitiFact_logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/PolitiFact_logo.svg/700px-PolitiFact_logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1119" data-file-height="193" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:PolitiFact_logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/PolitiFact.com" class="mw-redirect" title="PolitiFact.com">PolitiFact.com</a> was praised by rival fact-checker <a href="/wiki/FactCheck.org" title="FactCheck.org">FactCheck.org</a> and recommended as a resource to debunk fake news sites.</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Fact-checking_websites" class="mw-redirect" title="Fact-checking websites">Fact-checking websites</a> <a href="/wiki/FactCheck.org" title="FactCheck.org">FactCheck.org</a>, <a href="/wiki/PolitiFact.com" class="mw-redirect" title="PolitiFact.com">PolitiFact.com</a> and <a href="/wiki/Snopes.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Snopes.com">Snopes.com</a> authored guides on how to respond to fraudulent news.<sup id="cite_ref-snopesfieldguide_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-snopesfieldguide-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-factcheckhowtospot_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factcheckhowtospot-156">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-politifactletsfight_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-politifactletsfight-157">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> FactCheck.org advised readers to check the source, author, date, and headline of publications.<sup id="cite_ref-factcheckhowtospot_156-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factcheckhowtospot-156">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> They recommended their colleagues Snopes.com, <i>The Washington Post</i> Fact Checker,<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;b&#93;</a></sup> and PolitiFact.com.<sup id="cite_ref-factcheckhowtospot_156-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factcheckhowtospot-156">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> FactCheck.org admonished consumers to be wary of <a href="/wiki/Confirmation_bias" title="Confirmation bias">confirmation bias</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-factcheckhowtospot_156-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factcheckhowtospot-156">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> PolitiFact.com used a "Fake news" tag so readers could view all stories Politifact had debunked.<sup id="cite_ref-politifactletsfight_157-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-politifactletsfight-157">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> Snopes.com warned readers social media was used as a harmful tool by fraudsters.<sup id="cite_ref-snopesfieldguide_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-snopesfieldguide-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s "The Fact Checker" manager <a href="/wiki/Glenn_Kessler_(journalist)" title="Glenn Kessler (journalist)">Glenn Kessler</a> wrote that all fact-checking sites saw increased visitors during the 2016 election cycle.<sup id="cite_ref-kesslerfact_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kesslerfact-160">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> Unique visitors to The Fact Checker increased five-fold from the 2012 election.<sup id="cite_ref-kesslerfact_160-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kesslerfact-160">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> Will Moy, director of <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>-based fact-checker Full Fact, said debunking must take place over a sustained period to be effective.<sup id="cite_ref-kesslerfact_160-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kesslerfact-160">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> Full Fact worked with Google to help automate fact-checking.<sup id="cite_ref-googleishelping_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-googleishelping-161">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/FactCheck.org" title="FactCheck.org">FactCheck.org</a> former director Brooks Jackson said media companies devoted increased focus to the importance of debunking fraud during the 2016 election.<sup id="cite_ref-stelterfact_158-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stelterfact-158">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> FactCheck.org partnered with CNN\'s <a href="/wiki/Jake_Tapper" title="Jake Tapper">Jake Tapper</a> in 2016 to examine the veracity of candidate statements.<sup id="cite_ref-stelterfact_158-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stelterfact-158">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> Angie Drobnic Holan, editor of <a href="/wiki/PolitiFact.com" class="mw-redirect" title="PolitiFact.com">PolitiFact.com</a>, cautioned media companies chiefs must be supportive of debunking, as it often provokes <a href="/wiki/Hate_mail" title="Hate mail">hate mail</a> and extreme responses from zealots.<sup id="cite_ref-stelterfact_158-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stelterfact-158">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> In December 2016, PolitiFact announced fake news was its selection for "Lie of the Year".<sup id="cite_ref-biggestlie_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biggestlie-162">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kertscher_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kertscher-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> PolitiFact explained its choice for the year: "In 2016, the prevalence of political fact abuse \xe2\x80\x93 promulgated by the words of two polarizing presidential candidates and their passionate supporters \xe2\x80\x93 gave rise to a spreading of fake news with unprecedented impunity."<sup id="cite_ref-kertscher_36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kertscher-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> PolitiFact called fake news a significant symbol of a culture accepting of <a href="/wiki/Post-truth_politics" title="Post-truth politics">post-truth politics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-biggestlie_162-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biggestlie-162">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Google_CEO_comment_and_actions">Google CEO comment and actions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Google CEO comment and actions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_Google" title="Criticism of Google">Criticism of Google</a></div>\n<p>In the aftermath of the 2016 U.S. election, Google and Facebook, faced scrutiny regarding the impact of fake news.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTimes-GoogleFacebook-2016_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimes-GoogleFacebook-2016-163">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> The top result on Google for election results was to a fake site.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> "70 News" had fraudulently written an incorrect headline and article that Trump <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_elections_in_which_the_winner_lost_the_popular_vote" class="mw-redirect" title="United States presidential elections in which the winner lost the popular vote">won the popular vote</a> against Clinton.<sup id="cite_ref-wapo14november2016_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wapo14november2016-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-politifact14november2016_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-politifact14november2016-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYTimes-GoogleFacebook-2016_163-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimes-GoogleFacebook-2016-163">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> Google later stated that prominence of the fake site in search results was a mistake.<sup id="cite_ref-latimes16november2016_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimes16november2016-165">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> By 14 November, the "70 News" result was the second link shown when searching for results of the election.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTimes-GoogleFacebook-2016_163-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimes-GoogleFacebook-2016-163">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> When asked shortly after the election whether fake news influenced election results, <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> CEO <a href="/wiki/Sundar_Pichai" title="Sundar Pichai">Sundar Pichai</a> responded: "Sure" and went on to emphasize the importance of stopping the spread of fraudulent sites.<sup id="cite_ref-hartmans_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hartmans-166">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> On 14 November 2016, Google responded to the problem of fraudulent sites by banning such companies from profiting on advertising from traffic through its program <a href="/wiki/AdSense" class="mw-redirect" title="AdSense">AdSense</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-belfast_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-belfast-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-shanika_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shanika-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYTimes-GoogleFacebook-2016_163-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimes-GoogleFacebook-2016-163">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> Google previously had a policy for denying ads for dieting <a href="/wiki/Ripoff" title="Ripoff">ripoffs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Counterfeit" title="Counterfeit">counterfeit</a> merchandise.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> Google stated upon the announcement they would work to ban advertisements from sources that lie about their purpose, content, or publisher.<sup id="cite_ref-financialtimes_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-financialtimes-168">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> The ban is not expected to apply to <a href="/wiki/News_satire" title="News satire">news satire</a> sites like <i><a href="/wiki/The_Onion" title="The Onion">The Onion</a></i>, although some satirical sites may be inadvertently blocked under the new system.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTimes-GoogleFacebook-2016_163-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimes-GoogleFacebook-2016-163">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 25 April 2017, Ben Gomes wrote a blog post announcing changes to the search algorithms that would stop the "spread of blatantly misleading, low quality, offensive or downright false information."<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> On 27 July 2017, the <a href="/wiki/World_Socialist_Web_Site" title="World Socialist Web Site">World Socialist Web Site</a> published data that showed a significant drop after the 25 April announcement in Google referrals to left-wing and anti-war websites, including the <a href="/wiki/ACLU" class="mw-redirect" title="ACLU">ACLU</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alternet" class="mw-redirect" title="Alternet">Alternet</a>, and <a href="/wiki/CounterPunch" title="CounterPunch">Counterpunch</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/World_Socialist_Web_Site" title="World Socialist Web Site">World Socialist Web Site</a> insists that the "fake news" charge is a cover to remove anti-establishment websites from public access, and believes the algorithm changes are infringing on the democratic right to <a href="/wiki/Free_speech" class="mw-redirect" title="Free speech">free speech</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Facebook_deliberations">Facebook deliberations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Facebook deliberations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_Facebook" title="Criticism of Facebook">Criticism of Facebook</a></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Blocking_fraudulent_advertisers">Blocking fraudulent advertisers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fake_news_website&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Blocking fraudulent advertisers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mark_Zuckerberg_at_TechCrunch_SF_2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Facebook CEO Mark Zuckerberg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Mark_Zuckerberg_at_TechCrunch_SF_2013.jpg/170px-Mark_Zuckerberg_at_TechCrunch_SF_2013.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="259" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Mark_Zuckerberg_at_TechCrunch_SF_2013.jpg/255px-Mark_Zuckerberg_at_TechCrunch_SF_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Mark_Zuckerberg_at_TechCrunch_SF_2013.jpg/340px-Mark_Zuckerberg_at_TechCrunch_SF_2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="851" data-file-height="1299" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mark_Zuckerberg_at_TechCrunch_SF_2013.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Facebook CEO <a href="/wiki/Mark_Zuckerberg" title="Mark Zuckerberg">Mark Zuckerberg</a> specifically recommended fact-checking site <a href="/wiki/Snopes.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Snopes.com">Snopes.com</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>One day after Google took action, Facebook decided to block fake sites from advertising there.<sup id="cite_ref-shanika_31-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shanika-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYTimes-GoogleFacebook-2016_163-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimes-GoogleFacebook-2016-163">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> Facebook said they would ban ads from sites with deceptive content, including fake news, and review publishers for compliance.<sup id="cite_ref-financialtimes_168-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-financialtimes-168">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> These steps by both Google and Facebook intended to deny ad revenue to fraudulent news sites; neither company took actions to prevent dissemination of false stories in <a href="/wiki/Search_engine_results_page" title="Search engine results page">search engine results pages</a> or <a href="/wiki/Web_feed" title="Web feed">web feeds</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-belfast_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-belfast-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-paulblake_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-paulblake-173">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> Facebook CEO <a href="/wiki/Mark_Zuckerberg" title="Mark Zuckerberg">Mark Zuckerberg</a> called the notion that fraudulent news impacted the 2016 election a "crazy idea"<sup id="cite_ref-hall_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hall-174">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-frenkel_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-frenkel-175">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> and denied that his
